2:36:2386:0:14:72:354:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Reference-Dependent Job Search: Evidence from Hungary
2:37:2439:14:14:72:451:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Stefano DellaVigna, Attila Lindner, Balázs Reizer, and Johannes F. Schmieder
2:38:2515:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 22257
2:39:2543:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:May 2016
2:40:2551:14:28:72:175:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. D03,J64,J65
2:41:2570:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:42:2578:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:We  propose  a  model  of  job  search  with  reference-dependent  preferences,  where  the  reference 
2:43:2681:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:point is given by recent income. Newly unemployed individuals search hard given that they are at 
2:44:2777:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:a  loss, but  over  time  they  get  used  to  lower  income,  and  thus  reduce  their  search  effort.  In 
2:45:2885:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:anticipation of a benefit cut their search effort rises again, then declines once they get used to the 
2:46:2987:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:lower benefit level. The model fits the typical pattern of the exit from unemployment, even with 
2:47:3083:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:no  unobserved  heterogeneity. The  model  also  makes  distinguishing  predictions  regarding  the 
2:48:3182:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:response  to  benefit  changes,  which we  evaluate  using  a  unique  reform.  In  2005,  Hungary 
2:49:3280:14:14:72:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:switched from a single-step UI system to a two-step system, with unchanged overall generosity. 
2:50:3374:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:The system generated increased hazard rates in anticipation of, and especially following, benefit 
2:51:3471:14:14:72:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:cuts  in  ways  the  standard  model  has  a  hard  time  explaining.  We estimate  a  model  with  optimal 
2:52:3578:14:14:72:542:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:consumption and endogenous search effort, as well as unobserved heterogeneity. The reference-
2:53:3670:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:F:dependent  model  fits  the  hazard  rates  substantially  better  than  most  versions  of  the  standard 
2:54:3776:14:14:72:546:420:12:Times:12:Times:F:model. We estimate a slow-adjusting reference point and substantial impatience, likely reflecting 
2:55:3874:14:14:72:546:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:present-bias. Habit  formation  and  a  variety  of  alternative  models  do  not  match  the  fit  of  the 
2:56:3981:14:14:72:546:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:reference-dependent model.  We  discuss  one  model  which  also  fits  well,  but  is  at  odds  with 
2:57:4083:14:37:72:250:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:calibrated values and other evidence.
2:58:4120:37:14:72:167:341:12:Times:12:Times:C:Stefano DellaVigna
2:59:4138:14:14:72:239:327:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:C:University of California, Berkeley

2:72:4378:14:14:72:217:131:12:Times:12:Times:C:and CERS-HAS, IZA and IFS
2:73:4403:14:0:72:169:117:12:Times:12:Times:C:a.lindner@ucl.ac.uk
2:74:4422:0:14:315:381:341:12:Times:12:Times:C:Balázs Reizer
2:75:4435:14:14:315:441:327:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:76:4458:14:14:315:453:313:12:Times:12:Times:C:Central European University
2:77:4485:14:14:315:366:299:12:Times:12:Times:C:Nádor u 9.
2:78:4495:14:14:315:387:285:12:Times:12:Times:C:1051 Budapest
2:79:4508:14:14:315:357:271:12:Times:12:Times:C:Hungary
2:80:4515:14:14:315:393:257:12:Times:12:Times:C:and CERS-HAS
2:81:4527:14:28:315:442:243:12:Times:12:Times:C:reizer.balazs@krtk.mta.hu
2:82:4552:28:14:315:426:215:12:Times:12:Times:C:Johannes F. Schmieder
2:83:4573:14:14:315:441:201:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:84:4596:14:14:315:403:187:12:Times:12:Times:C:Boston University
2:85:4613:14:14:315:411:173:12:Times:12:Times:C:270 Bay State Road
2:86:4631:14:14:315:407:159:12:Times:12:Times:C:Boston, MA 02215
2:87:4647:14:14:315:355:145:12:Times:12:Times:C:and IZA
2:88:4654:14:14:315:390:131:12:Times:12:Times:C:and also NBER
2:89:4667:14:34:315:401:117:12:Times:12:Times:C:johannes@bu.edu
2:90:4682:34:0:72:444:83:12:Times:12:Times:C:A online appendix is available at http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w22257
3:91:4756:0:30:68:162:711:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:1  Introduction
3:92:4771:30:18:68:543:681:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Unemployment insurance programs in most Western countries follow a common design. The
3:93:4856:18:18:68:543:663:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits are set at a constant replacement rate for a fixed period, typically followed by lower
3:94:4951:18:18:68:543:645:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits under unemployment assistance. In such systems, the hazard rate from unemployment
3:95:5041:18:18:68:543:627:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:typically declines from an initial peak the longer workers are unemployed, surges at unemploy-
3:96:5135:18:18:68:543:609:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ment exhaustion, and declines thereafter. This has been shown in a variety of settings, such
3:97:5227:18:18:68:543:591:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:as in the United States (Katz and Meyer, 1990), Hungary (Micklewright and Nagy, 1999),
3:98:5313:18:18:68:543:573:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Austria (Card et al., 2007a), Slovenia (van Ours and Vodopivec, 2008), Germany (Schmieder
3:99:5402:18:18:68:323:555:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:et al., 2012a), and France (Le Barbanchon, 2012).
3:100:5451:18:18:85:543:537:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:It is well-known that a basic job search model a la Mortensen (1986) and van den Berg
3:101:5536:18:17:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(1990) is unable to match this pattern.  This model predicts an increasing exit hazard up
3:102:5625:17:18:68:543:502:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:until benefit expiration, with a constant exit rate thereafter. To match the time path, job
3:103:5716:18:18:68:543:484:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:search models add unobserved heterogeneity among workers. More productive workers are
3:104:5801:18:18:68:543:466:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:more likely to find a job initially, leading to a decrease in the hazard over time as the workers
3:105:5898:18:18:68:392:448:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:still unemployed are predominantly of the less productive type.
3:106:5961:18:18:85:543:430:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In this paper, we propose, and test, a behavioral model of job search which can account
3:107:6048:18:18:68:543:412:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for this time path of unemployment even in the absence of unobserved heterogeneity. Namely,
3:108:6139:18:18:68:543:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we incorporate one of the best established facts in psychology, that people’s perceptions and
3:109:6232:18:18:68:543:376:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:decisions are influenced by relative comparisons.  We assume that workers have reference-
3:110:6321:18:18:68:543:358:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependent preferences over their utility from consumption. As in prospect theory (Kahneman
3:111:6411:18:18:68:543:340:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and Tversky, 1979), workers are loss-averse with respect to consumption below a reference
3:112:6500:18:18:68:473:322:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:point. Further, we assume that this reference point is given by recent earnings.
3:113:6580:18:18:85:543:304:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:To fix ideas, consider a reference-dependent worker who was just laid off and assume,
3:114:6665:18:18:68:543:286:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for now, hand-to-mouth consumption.  At the time of job loss, the reference point of the
3:115:6753:18:17:68:543:268:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:unemployed is the previous wage, which is significantly higher than the unemployment benefit,
3:116:6846:17:18:68:543:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the new consumption level. The unemployed, therefore, finds the new state of unemployment
3:117:6935:18:18:68:543:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:particularly painful given the loss relative to the reference point, and so she searches hard at
3:118:7031:18:18:68:543:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the beginning of a UI spell. Over the weeks of unemployment, however, the reference point
3:119:7120:18:18:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shifts as the individual adapts to the lower benefit level, and the loss is thus mitigated. Hence,
3:120:7218:18:18:68:543:179:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the worker’s search effort decreases. As the end of the UI benefits draws near, the worker, if
3:121:7312:18:18:68:543:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:still unemployed, anticipates the loss in consumption due to the exhaustion of the benefits,
3:122:7404:18:18:68:543:143:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and searches harder. This force is at work also in the standard model, but it is heightened
3:123:7495:18:18:68:543:125:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:by the anticipation of the future loss aversion. If the worker does not find a job by the UI
3:124:7587:18:18:68:475:107:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:expiration, the worker once again slowly adjusts to the new, lower benefit level.
3:125:7668:18:18:85:543:89:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The hazard from unemployment for this reference-dependent worker decreases from the ini-
3:126:7756:18:0:68:543:71:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tial peak, increases at exhaustion, then decreases again. Hence, the predicted hazard matches
4:127:7850:0:18:68:465:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the patterns documented above, even in absence of unobserved heterogeneity.
4:128:7925:18:18:85:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:How would one distinguish the standard job search model from a reference-dependent
4:129:8007:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model? Consider two UI systems, the first offering a constant benefit path until periodT,
4:130:8096:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with the second offering higher initial benefits up to periodT1< Tbut lower benefits between
4:131:8188:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:T1andT(Figure 1a). The two systems have the same welfare benefit level after periodT.
4:132:8273:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The standard model with no heterogeneity predicts that, starting from periodT,the hazard
4:133:8361:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:rate in the two systems would be the same, as the future payoffs are identical (Figure 1b).
4:134:8452:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Furthermore, the hazard rate in the periods right before periodTwill be higher in the system
4:135:8544:18:18:68:379:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with two-step benefits given the lower benefits at that point.
4:136:8606:18:18:85:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The reference-dependent model makes three different predictions (Figure 1c). First, right
4:137:8695:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:after periodTthe hazard in the one-step system would be higher because of the higher loss
4:138:8784:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in consumption compared to the recent benefits. Second, this difference would attenuate over
4:139:8876:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:time and ultimately disappear as the reference point adjusts to the lower benefit level. Third,
4:140:8971:18:18:68:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the hazard rate in the first UI system increases alreadyin advance ofperiodT,in anticipation
4:141:9063:18:18:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the future loss aversion. Notice that, while these predictions are developed in the absence
4:142:9157:18:18:68:539:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of heterogeneity to highlight the intuition, we fully integrate heterogeneity in our estimates.
4:143:9252:18:18:85:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We evaluate a change in the Hungarian unemployment insurance system which is ideally
4:144:9336:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:suited for a test of the above predictions.  Before November 2005, the Hungarian system
4:145:9423:18:17:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:featured a constant replacement rate for 270 days, followed by lower unemployment assistance
4:146:9515:17:18:68:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits.  After November 2005, the system changed to a two-step unemployment system:
4:147:9600:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits are higher in the first 90 days, but lower between days 90 and 270, compared to the
4:148:9692:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:pre-period (Figure A-1). There was no major change in the unemployment assistance system
4:149:9780:18:18:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:taking place after 270 days.  As such, this UI set-up corresponds to the hypothetical case
4:150:9870:18:18:68:359:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:outlined above with periodTcorresponding to 270 days.
4:151:9923:18:18:85:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:An important feature of the Hungarian reform is that the total benefits paid out until day
4:152:10013:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:270 remain about the same after the reform. Hence, differences in savings and in selection in
4:153:10106:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the pre- and post- period are likely to be small, allowing for a more straightforward comparison.
4:154:10203:18:18:85:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We evaluate the reform by comparing the hazard rates into employment in the year before
4:155:10290:18:18:68:543:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and after the reform.  The evidence is well in line with the predictions of the reference-
4:156:10380:18:18:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependent model. In the weeks immediately preceding the 270-day exhaustion of benefits, the
4:157:10471:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:pre-reform hazard rates rise above the post-reform hazard rates. In the months following the
4:158:10563:18:18:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exhaustion, the pre-reform hazard rates remain higher, and they ultimately converge to the
4:159:10653:18:17:68:543:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:post-reform level only after a couple months. The observed pattern around the exhaustion is
4:160:10744:17:18:68:543:120:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consistent with the anticipation of, and then the direct effect of the higher loss in consumption
4:161:10841:18:18:68:543:102:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for individuals in the pre-reform. The ultimate convergence between the two hazards indicates,
4:162:10935:18:0:68:413:84:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in this interpretation, the timing of the reference point adjustment.
5:163:11005:0:18:85:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We present several robustness checks. Controlling for a broad set of controls and alternative
5:164:11098:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:definitions of our sample barely affects the estimated hazards. Also, an interrupted time series
5:165:11194:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:analysis shows that the break in the hazards occurs immediately in the quarter of introduction
5:166:11288:18:18:68:382:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of the reform, and does not appear to reflect previous trends.
5:167:11350:18:17:85:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:While the evidence is qualitatively consistent with predictions of the reference-dependent
5:168:11440:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model, it is important to compare the quantitative fit of the behavioral model with the fit of
5:169:11534:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the standard model allowing for unobserved heterogeneity. To do so, we structurally estimate
5:170:11626:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a model with optimal search effort, log utility, and unobserved heterogeneity in the form of
5:171:11718:18:18:68:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:types of individuals with different search costs.1Given that the reference-dependent model has
5:172:11812:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:two extra parameters (loss-aversion and updating horizon for the reference point), we allow
5:173:11903:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for one less cost type, two versus three in the standard model, thus equating the number of
5:174:11994:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimated parameters. We estimate the model with a minimum-distance estimator, matching
5:175:12081:18:18:68:512:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the empirical hazard rates in the pre- and post-reform to the predictions of the model.
5:176:12168:18:18:85:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The preferred estimate for the standard model does a relatively good job of fitting the
5:177:12255:18:18:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazards in the first 200 days. More specifically, the presence of heterogeneous types allows
5:178:12347:18:18:68:543:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to qualitatively match the spike in the hazard at 90 days post-reform. The standard model,
5:179:12437:18:18:68:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:however, is unable to capture the observed behavior leading up to, and following, the exhaus-
5:180:12530:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tion of benefits. In particular, the hazard rates from day 270 on in the pre- and post-period
5:181:12623:18:17:68:432:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are predicted to be almost identical, contrary to the empirical findings.
5:182:12696:17:18:85:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The reference-dependent model captures the spike at 90 days and the subsequent decrease,
5:183:12784:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:similar to the standard model (and with a closer fit). Importantly, this behavioral model also
5:184:12878:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:captures key features of the data which the standard model does not fit: the increase in
5:185:12966:18:18:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazard in the month prior to the expiration of benefits in the pre-period, the spike at 270
5:186:13057:18:18:68:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:days, the decrease thereafter, and the ultimate convergence of the hazard between the pre-
5:187:13147:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and post-period after a few months. The fit of the model is by no means perfect: the model
5:188:13237:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:underpredicts the spike at 270 days and the difference in hazards in the following two months.
5:189:13331:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Still, it captures most of the qualitative features which the standard model does not fit at all.
5:190:13428:18:18:85:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:An important caveat is that these estimates assume hand-to-mouth consumers. However,
5:191:13512:18:18:68:543:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:reference-dependent workers should build precautionary savings to smooth the upcoming loss
5:192:13602:18:18:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:utility due to a benefit decrease, eliminating the elevated hazards at benefit exhaustion. Thus,
5:193:13698:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the good fit of the reference-dependent model may depend crucially on an ad hoc assumption.
5:194:13789:18:18:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:To address this concern, in our benchmark estimates we incorporate a consumption-savings
5:195:13877:18:17:68:458:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:decision and estimate time preferences in addition to job search parameters.
5:196:13953:17:18:85:543:120:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The results point to an important interaction between reference dependence and impa-
5:197:14037:18:18:68:543:102:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tience. As the intuition above suggested, the reference-dependent model with optimal con-
5:198:14126:18:0:81:525:84:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:A:1For tractability, the model does not allow for a reservation wage choice, a restriction we revisit later.
6:199:14233:0:18:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sumption does not provide a good fit for the data if we impose high degrees of patience. Once
6:200:14326:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:we allow for estimated discount rates, however, the reference-dependent model fits the data
6:201:14417:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:well, as in the hand-to-mouth estimates. The point estimates indicate a significant weight
6:202:14507:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on gain-loss utility, slow updating of the reference point, and high impatience.  The stan-
6:203:14598:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dard model, with similarly high estimated impatience, fits the data significantly worse than
6:204:14690:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the reference-dependent model and in fact somewhat worse than the hand-to-mouth stan-
6:205:14775:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dard model.2Thus, the estimates with optimal consumption confirm the better fit of the
6:206:14861:18:18:68:459:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:reference-dependent model, and additionally point to the role of impatience.
6:207:14937:18:18:85:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:But are these estimates plausible? The estimate for loss aversion is in the range of the
6:208:15025:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:previous literature, but the estimated discount factor is arguably implausibly small at 0.9 for
6:209:15120:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a 15-day period, leading to an annual discount factor of 0.08 (The estimated discount factor
6:210:15212:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for the standard model is similarly small).  What appears to be extreme impatience may,
6:211:15299:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:however, reflect mis-specified time preferences.  Building on evidence in a large number of
6:212:15390:18:18:68:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:settings, including job search (DellaVigna and Paserman, 2005), we allow for present-biased
6:213:15481:18:18:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:time preferences (Laibson, 1997; O’Donoghue and Rabin, 1999), with an additional discount
6:214:15570:18:18:68:332:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:factorβbetween the current period and the future.
6:215:15619:18:18:85:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The estimates allowing for present bias do as well (in fact, attain a better fit) as the
6:216:15707:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimates with exponential discounting, but imply much more reasonable discounting. We
6:217:15793:18:17:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimate a present-bias parameterβ=0.58, well within the range of estimates in the literature,
6:218:15887:17:18:68:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for an implied annual discount factor of 0.52 for the first year and 0.88 for later years. The
6:219:15981:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:fit of standard model instead does not improve if we allow for present-bias preferences. Thus,
6:220:16075:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the evidence appears to point, not just to reference dependence, but also to impatience and
6:221:16166:18:18:68:308:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:likely present-bias among unemployed workers.
6:222:16211:18:18:85:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We then examine further the components of the reference-dependent model. The results do
6:223:16298:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:not depend on unobserved heterogeneity: a reference-dependent model with no heterogeneity
6:224:16387:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:provides nearly as good a fit. The results also do not depend on the exact reference-point
6:225:16477:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:updating rule, as the fit is similar with an alternative AR(1) updating assumption. Further,
6:226:16569:18:18:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the fit does not depend on allowing for gain utility (achieved at reemployment).  What is
6:227:16658:18:18:68:524:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:critical for the results, as expected, is that loss aversion experienced as income decreases.
6:228:16751:18:18:85:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:How does reference dependence compare to habit formation? Models a la Constantinides
6:229:16835:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(1990) and Campbell and Cochrane (1999), like the reference-dependent model, induce a
6:230:16920:18:18:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:temporarily higher marginal utility of income following a benefit cut as consumption gets
6:231:17009:18:17:68:543:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:closer to the habit. Thus, they could plausibly fit the patterns in the data. We highlight
6:232:17099:17:16:81:543:120:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:2In the hand-to-mouth case, the best fit for the standard model is for a relatively high degree of patience.
6:233:17207:16:12:68:543:104:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:Yet, for such level of patience, the workers should not go hand-to-mouth. Once we endogenize consumption,
6:234:17312:12:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:such estimates with high patience are not optimal any more, given that they would lead the workers to save
6:235:17418:12:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:and thus smooth the benefit jumps more than observed in the data. Thus, endogenizing the consumption
6:236:17518:12:0:68:488:68:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:decision is an important check for the ability of the standard model to fit the observed patterns.
7:237:17617:0:18:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a key difference. In the reference-dependent model, the impact of the loss on search effort
7:238:17708:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is approximately proportional to the size of the loss. Instead, in the habit-formation model
7:239:17800:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:larger decreases in consumption have disproportionate effects. Given this, the habit-formation
7:240:17894:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model underpredicts the spike in hazard at 270 days, since the benefit step-down at 90 days
7:241:17985:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is proportionally larger. We also estimate habit-formation models with multiplicative habits
7:242:18077:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:(e.g. Abel, 1990) that are equivalent to reference-dependent models with no loss aversion.
7:243:18167:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:These models provide a better fit than the standard model, though not quite as good as the
7:244:18257:18:18:68:479:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:reference-dependent model, confirming the role of loss aversion in our estimates.
7:245:18338:18:18:85:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Could alternative versions of the standard model fit the data as well as the reference-
7:246:18425:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependent model? We allow for, among other assumptions, different starting assets, back-
7:247:18513:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ground consumption, time-varying search costs, and a delay between search effort and the
7:248:18601:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:jobs start. We also estimate the model using different weights, using probability of exit in-
7:249:18694:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:stead of hazard, and excluding the spikes from the moments. None of these changes sizeably
7:250:18784:18:18:68:443:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:affect the fit of the standard model, or of the reference-dependent model.
7:251:18858:18:18:85:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We then examine alternative forms of unobserved heterogeneity. While in the benchmark
7:252:18943:18:18:68:543:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimates we assume heterogeneity in search cost in the spirit of Paserman (2008), we allow
7:253:19034:18:18:68:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for more cost types, for heterogeneity in re-employment wage, or in the search elasticity with
7:254:19128:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:respect to the returns to search. The first two forms of heterogeneity do not close the gap with
7:255:19224:18:17:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the reference-dependent model, but the model with heterogeneous search elasticity fits much
7:256:19315:17:18:68:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:better, even outperforming the reference-dependent model. This model explains the observed
7:257:19405:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:spikes by allowing for a type with such high search elasticity (over 50) that only searches once
7:258:19501:18:18:68:225:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits fall below a threshold.
7:259:19533:18:18:85:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:But is the model with heterogeneous search elasticity plausible? We provide two implica-
7:260:19621:18:18:68:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tions and two additional pieces of evidence which, in our view, cast doubt on it. First, this
7:261:19714:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model fits the data well only for very high elasticities; if we restrict the elasticities to be no
7:262:19812:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:higher than 5 (already quite high), the fit does not come close to matching the reference-
7:263:19902:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependent model. Second, given the high elasticities, the model makes the unlikely prediction
7:264:19995:18:18:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that, if welfare benefits were lowered, or increased, by just 10 percent, search effort would
7:265:20088:18:18:68:248:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:skyrocket, or conversely go to zero.
7:266:20124:18:18:85:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Further, we examine an earlier UI reform which lengthens the duration of unemployment
7:267:20209:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:assistance. The impact of the reform on the hazard path is very limited, mostly shifting the
7:268:20301:18:18:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:spike, consistent with out-of-sample predictions for the reference-dependent model. Instead,
7:269:20393:18:17:68:509:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the model with heterogeneous cost elasticity predicts a substantial dip in the hazards.
7:270:20480:17:18:85:543:120:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:We also compare the dynamic selection implied by the estimated models to the selection on
7:271:20569:18:18:68:543:102:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:observables in the data. We show that the selection implied by the standard model differs both
7:272:20663:18:0:68:543:84:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:qualitatively and quantitatively from the observed selection; instead, the implied selection is
8:273:20759:0:18:68:404:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:close to the observed selection for the reference-dependent model.
8:274:20825:18:18:85:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Finally, we briefly discuss other job search models which we do not estimate but which
8:275:20911:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:could potentially explain some of the findings. A model of storable offers (as in Boone and van
8:276:21006:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Ours 2012) could explain the spike in hazard at benefit exhaustion, but not the pattern of the
8:277:21100:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazards in the following months. A model of skill depreciation or screening (e.g. Schmieder
8:278:21191:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:et al., 2016) can explain decreasing hazards over the spell, but such decrease would plausibly
8:279:21285:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:be the same pre- and post-reform. Two classes of models which could potentially explain the
8:280:21376:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:findings are worker learning and consumption commitments (Chetty, 2003 and Chetty and
8:281:21461:18:18:68:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Szeidl, 2016). A worker may learn over time that finding jobs is harder than expected, and this
8:282:21556:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:learning may take place later in the pre-reform period, given the different benefit structure.
8:283:21650:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:A worker with committed consumption would increase search effort to avoid paying a fixed
8:284:21738:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:cost of adjustment; if despite this, she does not find a job soon enough, she will pay the cost
8:285:21833:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and then decrease search. These dynamics could generate some of the hazard patterns after
8:286:21922:18:18:68:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:day 270. While both models have intuitive features, unfortunately neither is tractable enough
8:287:22015:18:18:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to estimate on our sample.3For tractability reasons, we also do not estimate models with
8:288:22103:18:18:68:370:442:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:reservation wage choice and optimal consumption-savings.4
8:289:22160:18:18:85:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:To sum up, reference dependence, in combination with impatience, can help explain pat-
8:290:22246:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:terns in job search that are hard to rationalize with most alternative models, even allowing
8:291:22338:18:17:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for unobserved heterogeneity. These results have implications for potential redesigns of un-
8:292:22430:17:18:68:502:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:employment insurance policies, a point to which we return briefly in the conclusions.
8:293:22515:18:18:85:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The paper relates to the literature on unemployment insurance design (e.g. Chetty, 2008;
8:294:22603:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Kroft and Notowidigdo, forthcoming; Schmieder et al., 2012a).  Within this literature, we
8:295:22692:18:18:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:evaluate a unique reform: changing the time path of the benefit schedule, keeping the overall
8:296:22785:18:18:68:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:payments approximately constant. The paper is consistent with recent evidence of sharp con-
8:297:22876:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sumption drops at unemployment entry and UI exhaustion for unemployed workers (Ganong
8:298:22961:18:18:68:516:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and Noel, 2015; Kolsrud et al., 2015), suggesting approximate hand-to-mouth behavior.
8:299:23046:18:18:85:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The paper also contributes to a literature on behavioral labor economics, including work
8:300:23134:18:18:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on employer-employee gift exchange (Akerlof, 1982; Fehr et al., 1993; Gneezy and List, 2006),
8:301:23227:18:18:68:543:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:horizontal pay equity (Card et al., 2012; Breza et al., 2015), and target earnings in labor sup-
8:302:23323:18:18:68:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ply (Camerer et al., 1997; Farber, 2015). Within job search, DellaVigna and Paserman (2005)
8:303:23414:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consider the impact of present-bias while Spinnewijn (2013) examines the role of overconfi-
8:304:23505:18:17:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dence. We show that a reference-dependent model of job search makes unique predictions,
8:305:23592:17:16:81:543:138:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:3The consumption commitment model requires to keep track of a fixed cost decision, making the model
8:306:23691:16:12:68:543:122:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:cumbersome to estimate. To address this issue, Chetty (2003) makes the timing of fixed cost payment ex-
8:307:23794:12:12:68:543:110:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:ogenous. A consumption commitment model with exogenous consumption readjustment, as in Chetty (2003),
8:308:23895:12:8:68:204:98:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:would not explain our findings.
8:309:23926:8:16:81:543:90:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:4We present in the appendix estimates with reservation wage choice for the hand-to-mouth case.  The
8:310:24025:16:0:68:474:74:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:results should be considered only suggestive, as endogenizing consumption is very important.
9:311:24118:0:18:68:505:711:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:and that the data points to a combination of reference dependence and present bias.5
9:312:24202:18:18:85:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The paper also adds to the evidence on reference dependence from settings including
9:313:24285:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:insurance choice (Sydnor, 2010; Barseghyan et al., 2013), labor supply (Fehr and Goette,
9:314:24373:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:2007; Farber, 2015), domestic violence (Card and Dahl, 2011), goal setting (Allen et al.,
9:315:24462:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:forthcoming), and tax elusion (Engström et al., 2015; Rees-Jones, 2013). Across these settings,
9:316:24557:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the reference point is the status-quo, or the forward-looking expectation (Kőszegi and Rabin,
9:317:24650:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:2006). We estimate the speed of updating of a backward-looking reference point as in Bowman
9:318:24741:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:et al. (1999), similar to Post et al. (2008). This paper is also part of a literature on structural
9:319:24840:18:18:68:519:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:behavioral economics (Laibson et al., 2007; Conlin et al., 2007; DellaVigna et al., 2012).
9:320:24930:18:18:85:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The papers proceeds as follows. In Section 2, we present a model of job search and reference
9:321:25022:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependence. In Section 3 we present the institutional details and the data for the Hungary
9:322:25112:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:unemployment insurance reform, which we evaluate in Section 4. In Section 5 we present the
9:323:25202:18:36:68:329:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:structural estimates, and we conclude in Section 6.
9:324:25253:36:30:68:125:460:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:2  Model
9:325:25261:30:18:68:543:430:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In this section we present a discrete-time model of job search with reference-dependent prefer-
9:326:25356:18:18:68:543:412:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ences and present-biased preferences. We build on the job search intensity model presented in
9:327:25449:18:17:68:543:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Card et al. (2007a) and in Lentz and Tranaes (2005) by adding a reference dependent utility
9:328:25540:17:18:68:405:377:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:function in consumption with a backward looking reference point.
9:329:25604:18:18:85:543:359:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f5:A:Model Setup.As in Card et al. (2007a) we make two simplifying assumptions. First, jobs
9:330:25690:18:18:68:543:341:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:last indefinitely once found. Second, wages are exogenously fixed, eliminating reservation-wage
9:331:25785:18:18:68:543:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:choices. Each period a job seeker decides search effortst∈[0,1], representing the probability
9:332:25878:18:18:68:543:305:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:of receiving a job offer at the end of periodtand thus of being employed in periodt+ 1.
9:333:25965:18:18:68:543:287:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Search costs are given by the functionc(st), which we assume to be time-separable, twice
9:334:26053:18:18:68:478:269:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:continuously differentiable, increasing, and convex, withc(0) = 0andc′(0) = 0.
9:335:26131:18:18:85:544:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In each period individuals receive incomeyt, either UI benefitsbtor wagewt, and consume
9:336:26218:18:18:68:543:233:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:ct.  In the general model consumers smooth consumption over time by accumulating (or
9:337:26302:18:18:68:543:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:running down) assetsAt. Assets earn a returnRper period so that consumers face a per-
9:338:26387:18:18:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:period budget constraintAt+11+R=At+yt−ctand a borrowing constraintAt≥ −L. We also
9:339:26468:18:18:68:427:179:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consider a simplified model with hand-to-mouth consumption,ct=yt.
9:340:26533:18:18:85:543:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The direct utility from consumption in periodtfor an unemployed person isv(ct), where
9:341:26618:18:17:68:543:143:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:v(.)is an increasing and concave function. The novel aspect is the fact that the reference-
9:342:26709:17:19:68:543:126:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependent individual has, in addition to consumption utilityv(ct), also gain-loss utility. Fol-
9:343:26804:19:16:81:543:107:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:5Koenig et al. (2016) model a reference-dependent reservation wage choice in that the wage offers with
9:344:26906:16:11:68:543:91:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:some probability equal a previous wage (the reference). Their paper focuses on job matches and reservation
9:345:27012:11:0:68:358:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:wages, as opposed to on the dynamics of exit from unemployment.
10:346:27076:0:40:68:505:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:lowing the functional form of Kőszegi and Rabin (2006), flow utility in each period is
10:347:27162:40:0:176:227:671:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f14:?:u(ct|rt) =
10:348:27172:0:18:237:428:680:12:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f12:?:v(ct) +η[v(ct)−v(rt)]ifct≥rt
10:349:27200:18:0:237:428:662:12:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f12:?:v(ct) +ηλ[v(ct)−v(rt)]ifct< rt
10:350:27230:0:39:528:543:671:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:(1)
10:351:27233:39:18:68:543:632:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:wherertdenotes the reference point in periodt.The utility consists of consumption utility
10:352:27322:18:17:68:543:614:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:v(ct)and gain-loss utilityv(ct)−v(rt).  When consumption is above the reference point
10:353:27407:17:18:68:543:597:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:B:(ct≥rt), the individual derives gain utilityv(ct)−v(rt)>0, which receives weightη.
10:354:27489:18:18:68:543:579:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:When consumption is below the reference point (ct< rt), the individual derives loss utility
10:355:27580:18:18:68:543:561:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:v(ct)−v(rt)<0,with weightλη.The parameterλ≥1captures loss aversion: the marginal
10:356:27660:18:18:68:543:543:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:utility is higher for losses than for gains. This reference-dependent utility function builds on
10:357:27756:18:18:68:543:525:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:prospect theory Kahneman and Tversky (1979) without, for simplicity, modelling diminishing
10:358:27846:18:18:68:496:507:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:B:sensitivity or probability weighting. The standard model is a special case forη= 0.
10:359:27929:18:18:85:543:489:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The second key assumption is the determination of the reference pointrt.Unlike in the
10:360:28014:18:18:68:543:471:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:literature on forward-looking reference points (Kőszegi and Rabin, 2006), but in the spirit of
10:361:28108:18:18:68:543:453:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the tradition on backward-looking reference points (Bowman et al., 1999), the reference point
10:362:28201:18:37:68:345:435:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:is the average of income over theNprevious periods:6
10:363:28253:37:0:255:276:398:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f14:?:rt=
10:364:28256:0:16:293:299:406:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:?:1

10:369:28270:38:18:85:543:360:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:To gain perspective on the impact of reference dependence, consider an individual in
10:370:28354:18:18:68:543:342:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f6:B:steady state with consumption, income, and reference point equal toy. Then in periodT,
10:371:28440:18:18:68:543:324:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:consider a small, permanent decrease in income fromytoy−∆y  < y,and an identical
10:372:28520:18:18:68:543:306:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f14:B:decrease in consumption fromc=ytoy−∆y.7In periodT, utility changes tov(y−∆y) +
10:373:28598:18:18:68:543:288:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:ηλ[v(y−∆y)−v(y)].The short-term change in utility equals, up to a linear approximation,
10:374:28685:18:17:68:543:270:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f5:B:−(1 +ηλ) ∆y∗v′(y).Over time, however, the reference point adjusts toy−∆yso that the

10:376:28854:18:18:68:539:235:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Thus,ηλcaptures the weight on additional short-term utility in response to an income loss.

11:438:31520:18:18:68:543:163:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to our empirical setting. To build intuition and for tractability, we consider in detail the case

11:440:31707:18:18:68:543:127:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the general case. In the case of hand-to-mouth consumers, assets are not a control variable

12:467:32848:0:28:527:531:524:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f9:A:8

12:470:33022:18:18:85:543:461:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:a) In the standard model (η= 0), the search effort in all periods after benefit expiration at

12:483:33488:12:19:345:495:364:8:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f14:?:db1<0, fori= 0,1, ...N−1
12:484:33512:19:18:85:543:345:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Part a) is straightforward. In the standard model, the search decision depends exclusively
12:485:33602:18:18:68:529:327:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on future benefits and wages, and the reform leaves unaffected the benefits past period T.
12:486:33692:18:18:85:543:309:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The intuition for part b), which we prove in the appendix, is as follows. An increase in
12:487:33780:18:18:68:543:291:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:b1affects search effort in periodTthrough changes inVET+1andVUT+1. These value functions
12:488:33868:18:18:68:543:273:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are affected because frontloading the benefit path (increasingb1and reducingb2) will reduce
12:489:33959:18:18:68:544:255:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the reference point at timeT,rT, as long asN  < T. This will increase both the value of
12:490:34046:18:18:68:543:237:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:employment (due to an increase in gain utility) and the value of unemployment (due to a
12:491:34133:18:18:68:543:219:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:decrease in loss utility). Ifλ≥1the decrease in loss utility will be larger than the increase
12:492:34226:18:17:68:340:201:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in gain utility, leading to a reduction in search effort.
12:493:34283:17:18:85:543:184:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:These predictions are illustrated in Figures 1b) and c). In the standard model (Figure 1b),
12:494:34374:18:18:68:543:166:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:optimal search effort increases under both regimes up until periodT,and then plateaus after
12:495:34465:18:18:68:543:148:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:periodTat a level that is unaffected by the front-loading of benefits (Proposition 1a). Gener-
12:496:34559:18:18:68:543:130:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ally, the hazard rate for the front-loaded regime (the dotted red line) will be higher than the
12:497:34654:18:17:68:509:112:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:one for constant benefits in the periods right before periodT,given the moral hazard.
12:498:34739:17:15:81:543:95:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:8Note that search effort in periodtis not affected by UI benefits in periodt, since the individual will
12:499:34842:15:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:only start a job found in periodtin periodt+ 1. Thus search effortstcorresponds to the exit hazard from
12:500:34945:12:0:68:250:68:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:unemployment in periodt+ 1:st=ht+1.
13:501:34982:0:18:85:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In contrast, under reference dependence (Figure 1c), search effort in periodTis substan-
13:502:35070:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tially higher under the constant-benefit regime (continuous blue line).  Individuals in this
13:503:35162:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:regime experience a sharper drop in consumption and thus (forN < T) significant loss utility
13:504:35254:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:due to the higher reference point. Second, the difference in hazards persists but shrinks for
13:505:35347:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:B:Nperiods, at which point the reference point has fully adapted to the lower benefits under
13:506:35437:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:either regime, and thus search effort converges.  A third implication (not captured in the
13:507:35527:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Proposition) is that in the last few periods before periodT, for sufficiently large loss aver-
13:508:35621:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sionλ, the hazard is higher under the constant-benefit regime compared to the front-loaded
13:509:35711:18:18:68:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:regime. The anticipation of larger future losses under the constant-benefits regime generates
13:510:35804:18:18:68:520:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:this anticipatory effect, counteracting the moral hazard effect of more generous benefits.
13:511:35894:18:18:85:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Notice that Proposition 1 does not hold with either heterogeneity or optimal consumption.
13:512:35983:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:With heterogeneous types, differences in the path of benefits up to periodTmay lead to a
13:513:36071:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:different composition of types surviving at periodT,and thus differences in the hazard even
13:514:36162:18:18:68:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the standard model, violating Proposition 1a). However, given the assumption of constant
13:515:36253:18:18:68:450:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:total benefit payout, differences in type composition are likely to be small.
13:516:36330:18:18:85:543:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Introducing savings in the model also invalidates Proposition 1 since individuals may have
13:517:36420:18:18:68:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:different savings at periodT, thus creating differences in hazards, even under the standard
13:518:36511:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:model. However, given that the total benefit payments are constant, such differences in savings
13:519:36606:18:17:68:538:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:are likely to be small. We address both heterogeneity and savings in the estimation section.
13:520:36698:17:18:85:557:371:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f5:A:Present Bias.We extend the model by allowing for present-bias (Laibson, 1997; O’Donoghue
13:521:36786:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and Rabin, 1999), with an additional discount factorβ≤1between the current period and
13:522:36871:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the future. The present bias factorβinduces time inconsistency and fits behavior in a range of
13:523:36965:18:18:68:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:settings (see Frederick et al., 2002; DellaVigna, 2009). In the context of job search, DellaVigna
13:524:37062:18:18:68:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and Paserman (2005) solve for a job search model with present-biased preferences. We assume
13:525:37153:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:that individuals are naive about their future present-bias: they (wrongly) assume that in the
13:526:37246:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:future they will make decisions based on regular discountingδ. We make this assumption
13:527:37332:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:mostly for computational reasons, since the naive agent problem can be solved using the value
13:528:37425:18:18:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:functions of the exponential agent (given that the naive worker believes she will be exponen-
13:529:37518:18:18:68:543:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:tial from next period). In addition, the evidence on present bias is largely consistent with the
13:530:37614:18:18:68:273:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:naivete’ assumption (DellaVigna, 2009).
13:531:37653:18:32:85:497:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The naive hyperbolic discounting individual solves the following value functions:
13:532:37734:32:8:88:197:141:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f14:A:VU,nt(At)  =max

14:550:38242:37:30:68:215:575:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:3  Data and Institutions
14:551:38266:30:26:68:321:545:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:3.1  Unemployment Insurance in Hungary
14:552:38304:26:17:68:543:519:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Hungary had a generous two-tier unemployment insurance system up to 2005. In the first tier,
14:553:38396:17:18:68:543:502:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:potential duration and benefit amount depended on past UI contribution.9The maximum
14:554:38479:18:18:68:543:484:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:potential duration, obtained after around 4 years of contribution, was 270 days,10while the
14:555:38570:18:18:68:543:466:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefit level was based on the earnings in the previous year. After the exhaustion of first-tier
14:556:38666:18:18:68:543:448:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits, unemployment assistance (UA) benefits could be claimed in the second tier. The UA
14:557:38757:18:18:68:534:430:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefit amount was the same for everybody, with the potential duration depending on age.
14:558:38845:18:18:85:543:412:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:On May 30th, 2005 the Hungarian government announced a comprehensive reform of the
14:559:38927:18:18:68:543:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:UI system11, with the goal of speeding up transition from unemployment to employment. The
14:560:39016:18:18:68:543:376:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:government changed the benefit calculations formula in the first tier, but did not alter the way
14:561:39112:18:18:68:543:358:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:potential duration and the earnings base were calculated. Before the reform, the benefit in
14:562:39203:18:18:68:543:340:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the first tier was constant with a replacement rate of 65% and with minimum and maximum
14:563:39290:18:18:68:543:322:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefit caps. The reform introduced a two-step benefit system. For the first step, the length
14:564:39383:18:18:68:543:304:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:was half of the potential duration in the first tier, and at most 91 days, and the replacement
14:565:39477:18:17:68:543:286:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:was lowered to 60% with increased minimum and maximum benefit caps. For most claimants
14:566:39563:17:18:68:543:269:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:these changes meant lower benefits than under the old schedule. In the second tier everybody
14:567:39655:18:18:68:543:251:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:received the new minimum benefit amount, reducing benefits for most claimants compared to
14:568:39744:18:18:68:467:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:before. The benefit formula changes are summarized in Appendix Figure A-1.
14:569:39818:18:18:85:543:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The most prominent change occurred for those with 270 days of eligibility (four years of
14:570:39906:18:18:68:543:197:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:UI contributions before lay-off) and base year earnings above the new benefit cap (that is,
14:571:39997:18:18:68:543:179:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:they earned more than 114,000HUF ($570) per month in 2005). As Figure 2 shows, for this
14:572:40084:18:18:68:543:161:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:group the duration of benefits in the first tier remains 270 days. While in the old system the
14:573:40178:18:15:81:543:143:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:9Every worker in the formal sector must pay a UI contribution. In 2005, employers contributed 3% to the
14:574:40281:15:9:68:446:128:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:UI fund, while employees 1%. There is no experience rating of UI benefits in Hungary.
14:575:40366:9:15:77:543:119:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:10More specifically, potential benefit in the first tier was calculated as UI contribution days in the last 4
14:576:40475:15:9:68:249:104:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:years divided by 5, but at most 270 days.
14:577:40516:9:15:77:543:95:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:11The reform was part of a wider government program called “100 steps”.  Policies related to the labor
14:578:40618:15:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:market and unemployment insurance (such as reemployment bonus and training policies) are discussed later.
14:579:40723:12:0:68:464:68:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:In addition to that, VAT and corporate income tax were decreased from January 1st 2006.
15:580:40812:0:18:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:benefits were constant in the first tier, under the new rules benefits increased substantially
15:581:40906:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the first 90 days, but decreased afterwards. An important feature of the reform for this
15:582:40997:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:group is that the increase in weekly benefits in the first 90 days is about twice as large as
15:583:41090:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the decrease in weekly benefit between 90 and 270 days, keeping the total benefit pay-out for
15:584:41183:18:17:68:307:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:individuals unemployed for 270 days the same.
15:585:41228:17:18:85:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Even though the main element of the reform was the new benefit formula, there were
15:586:41310:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:other changes occurring at the same time.  Most notably, a reemployment bonus scheme
15:587:41394:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:was introduced with a bonus amount equal to 50% of the remaining total first-tier benefits.
15:588:41485:18:18:68:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:However, claiming the bonus was not without costs.  If the bonus was claimed, then the
15:589:41571:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:entitlement for the unused benefit days was nulled. This could be very costly for risk-averse
15:590:41664:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:agents or for those who could only find an insecure job. Also, the bonus could only be claimed
15:591:41758:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:after the date of first-tier benefit exhaustion. This meant hassle costs, since UI claimants had
15:592:41854:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:to show up and fill out the paper work in the local UI office. Given these costs, it is not
15:593:41945:18:18:68:543:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:surprising that the take-up rate of reemployment bonus was only 6%, making it unlikely that
15:594:42036:18:18:68:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:it had substantial effects. As a robustness check, we show that the results are not sensitive to
15:595:42132:18:18:68:371:442:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:dropping the reemployment bonus users from the sample.12
15:596:42188:18:18:85:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In addition to the introduction of the reemployment bonus, there were two other minor
15:597:42273:18:13:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:relevant changes. First, those who claimed UI benefit before February 5th, 2005 faced a longer
15:598:42367:13:22:68:543:393:8:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f5:B:13, but somewhat lower, benefit in the second tier.14To avoid this complication, we only focus
15:599:42461:22:18:68:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on those who claimed their benefits after February 5th, 2005.  Second, there were minor
15:600:42548:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:changes in financing training programs.15However, participation in training programs was
15:601:42636:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:very low (less than 5%) in our sample and our results are robust to dropping these claimants.
15:602:42729:18:18:85:543:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Those who exhausted benefits in both tiers (UI and UA) and were still unemployed could
15:603:42815:18:18:68:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:claim means-tested social assistance. The duration of social assistance is indefinite, while the
15:604:42911:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:amount depends on family size, family income, and wealth. In most cases social assistance
15:605:43000:18:16:77:543:263:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:12Lindner and Reizer (2015) investigate the reemployment bonus in detail and further show that it does not
15:606:43106:16:8:68:219:247:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:affect the unemployment duration.
15:607:43139:8:15:77:543:239:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:13Before the reform, the potential duration in the second tier was 270 days above age 45 and 180 days below
15:608:43246:15:12:68:543:224:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:45. Those who claimed UI after February 5th, 2005 were eligible for 180 days above age 50 and 90 days below
15:609:43353:12:9:68:160:212:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:50 in the second tier.
15:610:43375:9:15:77:543:203:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:14The change in the duration and benefit level in the second tier was introduced at November 1st, 2005
15:611:43477:15:12:68:543:188:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:at the same time as other changes. However, it affected everybody who claimed second tier (UA) benefits
15:612:43580:12:12:68:543:176:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:after November 1st, 2005. A UI claimant who claimed her benefits after February 5th, 2005 and had 270 days
15:613:43686:12:12:68:543:164:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:potential eligibility could only claim second tier benefits (UA) after November 1st, 2005. Therefore, claimants
15:614:43797:12:12:68:543:152:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:between February 5th, 2005 and November 1st, 2005 are under the old benefit system for the first tier, but
15:615:43903:12:8:68:343:140:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:face the same second tier (UA) insurance scheme, see Figure 3.
15:616:43965:8:16:77:543:132:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:15Unemployed participating in training programs received the so-called income substituting benefit. Be-
15:617:44068:16:12:68:543:116:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:fore November 1st, 2005 this amount was 22,200HUF ($111) or 44,400HUF ($222), depending on household
15:618:44168:12:12:68:543:104:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:characteristics and type of training. This benefit was payed in excess of the UI. After November 1st, the
15:619:44273:12:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:benefit was 34,200HUF ($171) for everybody, but the UI benefit was suspended during training. Although
15:620:44375:12:12:68:543:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:we only observe training participation after November 1st, 2005, aggregate data show that the probability of
15:621:44483:12:0:68:459:68:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:participation in training programs remained constant throughout this period Frey (2009).
16:622:44573:0:34:68:358:711:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:benefits are lower than the second tier UI benefit level.16
16:623:44632:34:26:68:127:677:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:3.2  Data
16:624:44641:26:18:68:543:651:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:We use administrative data17on social security contributions for roughly 4 million individuals
16:625:44735:18:18:68:543:633:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:between January 2002 and December 2008. The sample consists of a 50% de facto random
16:626:44819:18:18:68:543:615:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:sample of all Hungarian citizens who were older than 14 and younger than 75 in 2002.18The
16:627:44908:18:18:68:543:597:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:data contains information on UI claims from February 2004 to December 2008 as well as basic
16:628:44999:18:18:68:543:579:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:information used by the National Employment Service, like the starting and ending date of
16:629:45088:18:18:68:432:561:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the UI benefit spells and the earnings base used for benefit calculation.
16:630:45161:18:18:85:543:543:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:In this paper we only focus on UI claimants who are eligible for the maximum potential
16:631:45247:18:17:68:543:525:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:duration (270 days) in the first tier. In addition, we restrict our sample to those who are
16:632:45338:17:18:68:543:508:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:older than 25 years and younger than 49 years, since specific rules apply close to retirement.
16:633:45432:18:18:68:543:490:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Moreover, we identify as our main sample UI claimants with high earnings base, since our goal
16:634:45525:18:18:68:543:472:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:is to explore the variation in Figure 2. To construct a consistent sample over time, we focus
16:635:45618:18:18:68:543:454:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on the unemployed with earnings base above the 70th percentile among the UI claimants in a
16:636:45708:18:18:68:515:436:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:given year. In 2005, a UI claimant at the 70th percentile earned 100,800 HUF ($504).19
16:637:45794:18:18:85:543:418:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:To evaluate the reform, we construct two comparison groups of workers who entered UI
16:638:45878:18:18:68:543:400:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:just before or just after the reform, since the claiming date determined the relevant regime.
16:639:45971:18:18:68:543:382:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Due to the change in unemployment assistance in February 2005, we use all UI claimants
16:640:46057:18:18:68:543:364:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:between February 5th, 2005 and October 15, 2005 (to avoid getting too close to the reform)
16:641:46147:18:18:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:as our pre-reform group. For the post-reform group, we take UI entrants in the same date
16:642:46235:18:18:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:range (February 5 to October 15) in 2006 so as to match possible seasonal patterns. Figure 3
16:643:46327:18:18:68:543:310:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shows the timing of the two comparison groups and the range for which our data is available.
16:644:46419:18:18:68:543:292:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:For robustness checks, we later show results using data in the earlier and later ranges as well.
16:645:46515:18:17:85:543:274:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Table 1 shows basic descriptives for the two groups. The basic demographic characteristics,
16:646:46606:17:18:68:543:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:such as age at time of claiming, education and log earnings in the years 2002 - 2004, are similar
16:647:46703:18:18:68:543:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:before and after the reform. The waiting period (the number of days between job loss and the
16:648:46795:18:18:68:543:221:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:time of claiming UI benefits) is almost identical across the two groups, indicating that people
16:649:46890:18:18:68:543:203:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:towards the end of our before sample were not trying to delay UI claiming dates in order to
16:650:46981:18:18:68:543:185:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:become eligible to the new regime.20The take-up rates of the reemployment bonus scheme,
16:651:47068:18:15:77:543:167:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:16For large families, social assistance can be more generous than UI. However, social assistance cannot be
16:652:47174:15:9:68:380:152:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:claimed before all other benefits have been exhausted in the UI system.
16:653:47245:9:12:77:473:143:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:A:17The dataset is provided by the Institute of Economics - Hungarian Academy of Sciences.
16:654:47333:12:15:77:543:131:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:18More precisely the sample is composed of everybody born on the 1st of January, 1927, and every second
16:655:47436:15:9:68:295:116:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:day thereafter (3rd of January, 5th of January etc.).
16:656:47489:9:15:77:543:107:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:19Our results are robust to alternative earnings thresholds over time. For example, we estimated our main
16:657:47594:15:12:68:543:92:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:specifications for those whose (real) earnings base was above 114,000 HUF ($570) and obtained virtually the
16:658:47701:12:8:68:124:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:same results.
16:659:47714:8:0:77:543:72:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:20Appendix Figure A-2 shows the unemployment rate and GDP growth rate around the two periods in
17:660:47811:0:18:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:which was introduced in 2005, are quite low. Below we present robustness checks to address
17:661:47901:18:36:68:379:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the possibility that this bonus may have affected our results.
17:662:47963:36:29:68:222:657:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:4  Reduced Form Results
17:663:47986:29:26:68:244:628:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:4.1  Estimating Hazard Plots
17:664:48014:26:18:68:543:602:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:In this section, we evaluate the impact of the reform on the exit rates from unemployment. We
17:665:48107:18:18:68:543:584:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimate the hazard rates with a linear probability model separately for each 15-day period21,
17:666:48201:18:36:68:342:566:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:indexed byt, after entering unemployment insurance:
17:667:48252:36:26:185:543:530:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:A:I(t∗i=t|t∗i≥t) =β0,t+β1,tP OSTi+Xiγ+ǫit,(8)
17:668:48295:26:18:68:543:504:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:whereiindexes individuals andt∗irepresents the duration of unemployment of individuali.
17:669:48382:18:18:68:543:486:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The left hand side is an indicator for individualifinding a job in periodt, conditional on
17:670:48472:18:18:68:543:468:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:still being unemployed at the beginning of the period. The variableP OSTiis an indicator
17:671:48560:18:18:68:543:450:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for individualiclaiming benefits in the post-reform period, whileXiis a matrix of control
17:672:48649:18:17:68:543:432:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:variables. The equation is estimated separately for each periodton the sample of individuals
17:673:48741:17:18:68:543:415:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:who are still unemployed at timet(that is conditional ont∗i≥t). The estimates forβ0,tare
17:674:48829:18:18:68:543:397:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimates for the hazard function in the pre-period, while the estimates forβ1,trepresent the
17:675:48922:18:18:68:543:379:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:shift of the hazard function between the before and after period. In our baseline estimates we
17:676:49016:18:35:68:527:361:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:do not control for any observablesXi, and show results controlling forXias robustness.22
17:677:49104:35:26:68:171:326:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:4.2  Main Result
17:678:49120:26:17:68:543:300:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:Figure 4a) shows the estimates of equation (8) for eachtwith no controls.  The blue line
17:679:49208:17:18:68:543:283:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:represents the coefficient estimates ofβ0,t, the estimated hazard function in the before period,
17:680:49304:18:18:68:543:265:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:while the red line represents the estimatedβ0,t+β1,t, the after period hazard. Vertical lines
17:681:49397:18:22:68:539:247:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:indicate that the difference between the two series is statistically significant at the 5% level.
17:682:49494:22:12:68:543:225:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:Hungary. The unemployment rate was quite stable at around 7.5 percent during and after the two sample
17:683:49595:12:12:68:543:213:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:periods. GDP growth was also stable during the sample periods, only slowing down at the beginning of 2007.
17:684:49701:12:12:68:543:201:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:Below we show extensive robustness checks, showing that our results are not driven by changes in the economic
17:685:49810:12:12:68:543:189:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:environment that occurred later and that the shape of the hazard rates are in fact very stable over time except
17:686:49921:12:8:68:276:177:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:for the exact point when the UI policy changes.
17:687:49968:8:15:77:543:169:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:21We choose a 15-day period so that the benefit path steps after 90 days and 270 days occur at integer
17:688:50070:15:9:68:493:154:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:values of these periods. The results are very similar with hazards computed at 7 days or 30 days.
17:689:50167:9:15:77:543:145:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f11:F:22Note that these hazard functions should not be viewed as consistent estimates at the individual level,
17:690:50271:15:12:68:543:130:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:but rather as estimates of the average hazard function in the population.  While the natural experiment,
17:691:50375:12:12:68:543:118:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:assuming the conditional independence assumption holds, identifies the causal effect of the reform on the
17:692:50480:12:12:68:543:106:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:average population hazard function, the shape of this average hazard function is potentially affected by duration
17:693:50593:12:12:68:543:94:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:dependence or by changes in selection due to the reform. While we address differential selection in our reduced
17:694:50704:12:12:68:543:82:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:form results section by comparing the estimated hazards controlling and not controlling for observables, an
17:695:50811:12:0:68:527:70:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f11:F:important aspect of our structural estimation below will be to explicitly model unobserved heterogeneity.
18:696:50918:0:18:85:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The exit rate from unemployment in the pre-reform period shows a familiar pattern for a
18:697:51005:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:one-step unemployment system. The exit hazard falls in the first months after entering UI,
18:698:51095:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:then it increases as it approaches the exhaustion point of UI benefits (at 270 days). After
18:699:51186:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:this exhaustion point, it falls and spikes again as people exhaust the second tier benefits,
18:700:51278:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:unemployment assistance, at 360 days.  The hazard rate then decreases monotonically, as
18:701:51365:17:18:68:363:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:unemployed people are only eligible for welfare programs.
18:702:51422:18:18:85:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The exit hazard changes substantially after the introduction of a two-step system. The
18:703:51508:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazard rate increases at 90 days, at the end of the higher unemployment insurance benefit,
18:704:51598:18:18:68:543:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and remains elevated compared to the pre-reform period for the following 2.5 months. By
18:705:51685:18:18:68:543:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:180 days, the pre- and post-reform hazards have converged, and both hazards increase at the
18:706:51776:18:18:68:543:532:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exhaustion of UI benefits at 270 days. Importantly though, the post-reform hazard increases
18:707:51867:18:18:68:543:514:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:significantly less, and the pre-reform hazard remains significantly higher for three months
18:708:51958:18:18:68:543:496:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:following UI exhaustion. Finally, by 360 days, the end of unemployment assistance, the two
18:709:52048:18:18:68:249:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazards have once again converged.
18:710:52082:18:18:85:543:460:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The most striking difference occurs around day 270, when in the pre-reform period the
18:711:52167:18:18:68:543:442:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:exit hazard remains significantly higher after the UI exhaustion point (270 days) relative to
18:712:52260:18:18:68:543:424:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the post-reform period. As we discussed above, this difference in hazards is hard to reconcile
18:713:52354:18:18:68:543:406:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:with the standard model: from day 270 onwards, the benefit levels are identical in the pre-
18:714:52445:18:17:68:543:388:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and post-period, and in addition the total amount of benefits received up to day 270 is also
18:715:52537:17:18:68:543:371:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:almost identical. Hence, in the standard model we would expect similar hazards (even with
18:716:52626:18:18:68:543:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:heterogeneity, as we show below).  A modified standard model with storable offers could
18:717:52713:18:18:68:543:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:potentially match the spike at 270 days, but it still does not explain the persistent difference
18:718:52809:18:18:68:307:317:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:in the hazards after the exhaustion of benefits.
18:719:52857:18:18:85:543:299:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:The difference in hazards instead fits nicely with the reference-dependent model: the work-
18:720:52948:18:18:68:543:281:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:ers in the pre-reform period experience a larger drop-off in benefits around day 270, inducing
18:721:53042:18:18:68:543:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:a spike in loss utility and thus an increase in the value of search. The persistence for three
18:722:53136:18:18:68:543:245:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:months of the higher hazard indicates slow adjustment of the reference point. Furthermore,
18:723:53226:18:18:68:543:227:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the increase in hazard in the pre-period happens already in anticipation of benefit expiration
18:724:53320:18:18:68:370:209:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:at day 270, consistent with the reference-dependent model.
18:725:53378:18:18:85:543:191:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:While we focus mainly on the hazard rate around day 270 because it leads to the most
18:726:53462:18:18:68:543:173:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:distinct predictions, the observed patterns around day 90 are also consistent with reference
18:727:53554:18:18:68:543:155:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:dependence. The spike in the hazard at 90 days in the post-period, corresponding to the first
18:728:53647:18:17:68:543:137:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:step down in benefits, disappears after 3-4 months, consistent once again with loss utility
18:729:53738:17:18:68:543:120:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:and a slowly-adjusting reference point. However, the spike itself in this period could also be
18:730:53832:18:18:68:496:102:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:explained by the standard model with unobserved heterogeneity, as we show below.
18:731:53912:18:0:85:543:84:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Figure 4b) shows the estimated survival function for the two groups.  We obtain these
19:732:53999:0:18:68:543:711:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:estimates using a variant of equation (8), where we estimate the equation again pointwise
19:733:54088:18:18:68:543:693:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:for alltbut including the whole sample and takingP(t∗i≥t)as the outcome variable. The
19:734:54173:18:18:68:543:675:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:survival functions diverge after 90 days, with lower survival probabilities in the after group
19:735:54267:18:18:68:543:657:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:than in the before group.  This difference persists until around 300 days, after which the
19:736:54357:18:17:68:543:639:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:two lines converge. Since the expected duration in unemployment is simply the integral over
19:737:54448:17:18:68:543:622:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the survival function from 0 onwards, the expected unemployment duration is significantly
19:738:54537:18:18:68:543:604:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:reduced in the after period. It is striking that even though the reform made the UI system
19:739:54627:18:18:68:543:586:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:more generous on average (since short term unemployed received more benefits, while the
19:740:54714:18:35:68:490:568:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:long-term unemployed received about the same), the expected duration decreased.
19:741:54793:35:26:68:211:533:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:4.3  Robustness Checks
19:742:54815:26:18:68:543:507:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:The results presented so far do not control for demographic characteristics. Even though the
19:743:54907:18:17:68:543:489:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:differences in demographics between the pre- and the post-period are quite small (Table 1),
19:744:54998:17:18:68:543:472:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:they could potentially explain differences in the hazard patterns over time if the demographic
19:745:55092:18:18:68:543:454:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:impacts on the hazard rates are large. Thus, we re-estimate equation (8) controlling for a rich
19:746:55187:18:18:68:543:436:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:set of observable characteristics, where we allow these characteristics to have arbitrary effects
19:747:55284:18:18:68:543:418:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:on the hazard function at each point, the only restriction being that the effect is the same in
19:748:55379:18:18:68:543:400:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:the before and after period. As Figure 5a) shows, controlling for observables has virtually no
19:749:55473:18:18:68:456:382:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:B:effect on the hazard rates, implying that they cannot explain our findings.23
19:750:55550:18:18:85:543:364:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:A separate concern regards the introduction of the reemployment bonus in November 1st,
19:751:55636:18:18:68:543:346:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:2005. While the take-up rate of the bonus was just 6% in our sample, it may still affect the
19:752:55728:18:18:68:543:328:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:hazard rate in the post-reform period, especially in the first 90 days. As a check, we drop
19:753:55819:18:18:68:543:310:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:B:all individuals that received a reemployment bonus and estimate our baseline specification on
